Oil Market

Flowers and Women's Rights

— Zhan Lu

The unshakeable old-style pharmacists, whenever they compounded medicine, always adhered to the traditional ideas of thousands of years, which was to refuse "chickens, dogs, and women" entry. Similar to the Westerners' former parks, which didn't allow "dogs and Chinese" entry, it was the same kind of insult. Therefore, I believe that the avoidance of "chickens, dogs, and women" during medicine compounding is a barbaric habit that violates women's rights and must be overthrown.

Although the promotion of women's rights in the 20th century is said to be a matter of human effort, isn't it also the will of heaven? I see that in the natural world, many kinds of flowers and plants speak up for women, so I understand that promoting women's rights is the will of heaven.

First, there are orchids. The secret to growing orchids is that every morning, you must wipe them with a comb that has hair oil and grime on it. Then the flowers will bloom fragrantly, especially with a woman's hand, which is most suitable. The Master of Huainan said: "If a man plants orchids, they are beautiful but not fragrant, their feelings do not intertwine." It can be seen that orchids are close to women and disgusted with men. If China had a female president or female chairman, then orchids, which advocate for women's rights, would definitely be necessary to be considered as the national flower. Second, there is the "afraid of wife grass". This grass comes from Si'en Prefecture in Guangxi. As the name suggests, it can represent the authority of wives. Each plant produces more than ten leaves, shaped like a phoenix tail, and the flowers are light yellow, growing on the corner of walls. If it gets close to a man, the leaflets will move on their own; as long as a woman steps forward and shouts, the grass becomes timid and dare not move! Fearing women and not fearing men is the characteristic of "afraid of wife grass."

Third, there is the "female fragrant, male stinky grass". There is a passage recorded in the Jian Gu Ji, which roughly says: "This grass, when worn by women, smells fragrant for several miles; when worn by men, it produces a strange odor. In the past, a husband on the sea picked up this grass, disliked its stench, and discarded it. A woman picked it up, and the grass became very fragrant; the man followed her, wanting to take back the grass; the woman ran quickly, and he couldn't catch up. Therefore, it is said: 'If you want to know that a woman is strong, turning stench into fragrance.'" In the past, when I read Dream of the Red Chamber, I saw Lin Daiyu often scolding men as smelly men, and I thought it was Lin Daiyu's arbitrary judgement. Now I understand that Lin Daiyu's words also have a basis. I guess she read this story of "female fragrant, male stinky grass", so she gave the men the epithet of "stinky." Furthermore, in the market, in cheap silk shops and foreign goods stores, whenever female customers, especially modern women, come to the door, the shop assistants are willing to give an extra inch or two. If male customers come to the door, they cannot get such rights. I think these shop assistant gentlemen are probably incarnations of "female fragrant, male stinky grass." Hehe.

Elixir of Immortality

— Xu Jie

Please have the eaves-flying, wall-walking, acupoint-striking, and sword-immortal experts hired by our esteemed country fight against the Japanese soldiers who wear the Taishang Laojun's "Hurry, hurry, as the statutes command!" talisman, or the divine soldiers who have eaten the elixir of immortality researched by Mr. Moriichi Tsuchida of Osaka University. In the end, who will lose and who will win, we can only wait for the next installment.

Flying eaves, walking walls, striking acupoints, and sword immortals are the treasures of our national essence: "Hurry, hurry, as the statutes command!" The divine talisman and the elixir of immortality of Qin Shi Huang are also our national essence, but they were stolen by the Japanese and made into magic weapons. With a flash of sword light and a shout of "hit", I don't know if it can kill the Japanese soldiers wearing the divine talisman? With a point of two fingers, I don't know if it can kill the Japanese who have eaten the elixir of immortality? Each showing their expertise, it's quite a sight to see! Of course, the League of Nations, after seeing it, will gnash their teeth, shiver, and turn pale. Therefore, there will be no Second World War. The Far East will not have any storms, wouldn't it all be thanks to the magic weapons?

According to the Tokyo Asahi Shimbun: "Qin Shi Huang sent Xu Fu to Japan to seek the elixir of immortality. Xu Fu arrived in Japan and worked hard to study it. As a result, he invented a kind of immortal medicine. The principle of this medicine has been researched by Mr. Moriichi Tsuchida of the Brewing Department of the Faculty of Engineering of Osaka University, and its ingredients are known to be: (1) Ginseng (2) Cloves (3) Fennel (4) Branch Orchid (5) Angelica sinensis (6) Rhubarb (7) Chuanxiong, etc., combined together. Mr. Tsuchida has created a kind of longevity wine and is testing it in the Brewing Laboratory of the Faculty of Engineering, making a strange and fragrant medicinal wine." Ha! Ha! The Japanese really know how to play tricks. I believe this news has two effects: (1) To anesthetize their soldiers, and has the same eye-stimulating effect as the "divine talisman." (2) To anesthetize the ignorant Chinese people, to promote their medicinal materials. Jilin ginseng originally didn't have much tonic effect, it was only used by our esteemed country's merchants to deceive and make money. The leakage of Korean ginseng is about millions per year, and now with the addition of ginseng leakage, it is even more alarming. Furthermore, eating a large amount of fennel is poisonous, rhubarb causes diarrhea, chuanxiong and angelica are just for promoting blood circulation. Eating this "elixir of immortality" may not necessarily lead to immortality, I'm afraid it will lead to a quick death!

After the Japanese die, they are all "cremated", and the warlords and chaebols are all just a pinch of "dust"! If this elixir of immortality is really effective, then building fences under the sea, reclaiming land, and invading foreign countries would be especially important for them. Let me copy a poem:

Morality of the Three Sovereigns and Five Emperors, fame of the Xia, Shang, and Zhou dynasties, heroes of the Five Hegemons made a ruckus in the marketplace, and power rose and fell in an instant.

How many lines of names in the history books? Countless barren mounds in Beiman Mountain! Our ancestors worked the land, and now we reap the rewards. What's there to say about the dragon and tiger fights!

Today to Hong Temple

— Ke Ding'an

Waking up early every day is my habit. The weather these few days has been very mild, and it's especially easy to get up in the morning. Today, I came out of my residence and walked west along Nanjing Road, intending to go to Jing'an Temple Road. Who knew that when I reached the Sidu Temple (commonly known as Hongli), I looked inside and saw that the incense was very prosperous. Suddenly, I remembered that today was the fifteenth day of the fourth month of the lunar calendar. Our general public (the government is implementing the Gregorian calendar, but you are complying in appearance but opposing in reality, "going your own way") taking the small to compare to the big, it is conceivable that there are countless followers of this kind of conservatism, especially in Shanghai.

Walking into the Sidu Temple, I used a calm gaze to observe the general pilgrims and analyze them, and I got the following kinds: (1) the unemployed, (2) the disturbed (the above belong to men), (3) those who take burning incense as a matter of duty, (4) those who hope that the gods will bless the development of their XX business, (5) those who are escorted (the above belong to women), and many others that are inexplicable.

The unemployed people's expressions seem to hang their entire chaotic thoughts. When he puts his head on the prayer mat with sincerity, and thinks of the respect of more than three kneelings and five kowtows, at least he is unemployed now.

The wavering state of those who are restless is also very obvious. When he is holding a lottery ticket in his hand, staring intently with both eyes, probably this lottery ticket must be a low one!

Those who take burning incense as a matter of duty, this is another kind of woman. They have a yellow cloth bag hanging around their waists, meaninglessly writing the name of X family in X village, and below it is written in larger letters: "Pilgrimage to Mount." I really don't know what "mountain" they are visiting? There is also a young woman, with a big "Buddha" character written on the yellow cloth bag hanging on her, and that Buddha character just happened to be covering the lower part of her waist. I think "if the Buddha has a spirit, he should also cry injustice."

Generally speaking, business women are wearing modern coats and holding an old 18th-century incense basket in their hands. When they bow down, they seem to be silently chanting something in their small mouths! This must be secretly praying to the gods for the development of their business.

There are also some who are escorted, and their expressions are very ugly, their hair is disheveled like messy grass, and their faces are withered and yellow like broken wax. They also mechanically insert incense and light candles; I see them as if they are in a dream.

There is also a young man wearing a suit who is also kneeling and kowtowing. This should belong to the "restless" category.

Using an average estimate, each person spends half a dollar on: Yuanbin sandalwood, candles, paper ingots, scriptures, etc. In that one hour, there were: forty-three old women, seventy-six young women, fifty-one middle-aged women, twenty-three young men, nineteen old men and old women, and other children who came along and onlookers like me are not counted.

Looking at the red-hot furnace and the smoke curling up, I thought of the great battle in Luan East, which made people shudder!

Correction: In yesterday's article selling children, the fourth character "小" (small) in the title was a misprint of the character "子" (child).

Short Story

Drafted into the Army (Part 2)

— Tian Hensheng

"What can we do? It's not just one family's business. There must be many people in our village who should be drafted. How can we come up with a solution!"

"If there's no solution, are we just going to let him go? Once he leaves, when will he come back? Will he be able to come back? Heavens!" She couldn't help but cry out of disappointment again, leaning on the table, no longer asking Old Man Yang to come up with a solution. She was hopeless!

Old Man Yang originally loved this daughter. When she was unmarried, she got whatever she wanted, and he never wanted to disappoint her. This time, she encountered something he couldn't do anything about, but it was related to his daughter's life, and he didn't have a son himself, and he would have to rely on this son-in-law to take care of him in the future. Suddenly, her son-in-law was drafted into the army. How could he not feel heartbroken! At this time, hearing his daughter say "Will he be able to come back?", he immediately realized: This fighting is such a dangerous thing, guns and cannons have no eyes, and his son-in-law's departure is mostly ominous! But he couldn't say these words to his daughter, and for a moment he didn't have any words to comfort his daughter, so he had to let her cry miserably!

The aunt came in from outside, and she wasn't surprised to see this situation. She already knew that her niece must be crying because her niece's husband was drafted into the army; and she had already seen four or five families crying in the same way. Although she felt pity, she didn't feel as much pain as Old Man Yang. She had a different kind of psychology. Seeing other people's families crying, it was as if the pent-up resentment that other people's families had intentionally or unintentionally given her was vented, and the feeling of injustice subsided. That was because she had no sons and no daughters.

Old Man Yang was sighing with his head down, and Gou Guniang was crying. They didn't even notice the aunt entering the door.

"Oh dear! Gou Guniang is also crying because of the draft, right? What a sin! But, what's the use of just crying!" The aunt originally didn't have sympathy, and Gou Guniang knew it too. Moreover, she didn't like this aunt when she was unmarried. Hearing these words, she didn't raise her head.

Old Man Yang wasn't answering the aunt either, he was just talking to himself, "Sigh! What a sin! Why did the war start for no reason! Chen Laowu came back from the city and talked about the fighting outside. He said it was very far from here, so why did they come here to draft soldiers? Could it be that the people who were fighting have already been killed!"

"My aunt's family is also crying in a mess!" the aunt said.

Old Man Yang seemed surprised, looked at the aunt, and said, "Doesn't she only have two sons?"

"Even with two, one has to be drafted!"

"Did she agree to let him be drafted?"

"How could she not agree. A'gui's courage isn't small, he's not afraid, saying that he can't get out of it, so he'll just go, it's not like going there means death. But A'gui's wife is crying even harder than our Gou Guniang!"

"That's understandable!" Old Man Yang nodded.

"There's no need to cry like that!" The aunt was feeling another kind of injustice: "She didn't try to stop A'gui, but she grabbed onto my aunt, wanting my aunt to not allow A'gui to go; if A'gui went, she would ask my aunt for a husband, which made my aunt even more embarrassed!"

"What's going to happen now?"

"A'gui hasn't left yet, and she's already so unreasonable, crying and rolling on the ground, wanting my aunt to watch over her husband for her. When A'gui leaves in the future, won't she be even more clingy to my aunt? My aunt has spoiled this daughter-in-law too much in the past, and now she's climbing on top of her mother-in-law. She's afraid that her daughter-in-law will make trouble in the future, so she's trying to find a way to leave!"

"What can we do?" Old Man Yang was very strange, and asked the aunt in return.

"You should also help me find a way!" Gou Guniang suddenly jumped up, grabbed Old Man Yang's hand, and pushed him, saying: "If Aunt can find a way, then you can also find a way for me. Dad, do you think I'm easy to talk to? If Xiao Niu is drafted, I'll also ask you for a husband!" Gou Guniang suddenly also became unreasonable, but she didn't cry. But her unreasonableness was different from A'gui's wife, she was being coquettish.

Novel

The Art of Business (12)

Tea Parties in the Hardware Industry

Tea Party Time

Those in the hardware industry who do tea party business are called "tea party runners". The goods they sell are all hardware products in the construction category. There are about fifteen or sixteen companies in the local industry that do tea party business. The larger ones are Yuanzhuang, Xinrenchang, Yuanyang, Yuansheng, etc. The time is from 4 pm to 8 pm. Their route is from 4 pm to 6 pm at Touji Bridge Luochun Pavilion Tea House, and from 6 pm to 8 pm at the Great Ma Road Tongyu Spring, Yile Tian, and Si Ma Road Changle Tea House. In addition, Tianchan on Si Ma Road and Guihua Hall in the city are available at any time. Therefore, the largest market is the Luochun Pavilion Tea House. The number of people who come there includes foreign firms, construction lumber companies, and fellow industry companies. They negotiate the price of goods with foreign firms. They talk about the price of slow-moving goods with fellow industry and domestic companies. Construction companies only discuss the location where they are needed and the goods that are needed. However, they do not discuss the price level. The price is filled in on the invoice when the goods are delivered (usually three or four cents to one or two taels higher than the market price). Payment procedures are either at the end of the small or large month, or after the landlord receives the payment, or only once a month, or there are also cash payments. Therefore, the price level has to fluctuate accordingly.

The salespeople who run tea parties in the industry are called "tea party runners". The managers who run tea parties are called "upper tea parties". They have to pay a tea fee of one yuan per person. As for the hardware products in terms of business, there are dozens of varieties such as bamboo steel, cement, triangular iron, steel wire mesh, new ocean yuan, French West fasteners, corrugated iron oil wool felt, etc. There are also large transactions for asphalt.

Tea Shop Business

There are about five tea shop groups in Shanghai, including Anhui, Jiangxi, Fujian, Hangshao, and Guangdong. The most powerful is the Anhui group, followed by the Hangshao group. The hardware products they handle are only four kinds: small green lead bars, number two white lead sheets, ten-pound tinplate, and one-inch two-point five French West needles. Tea shops call white lead sheets zinc sheets or zinc skins. Tinplate is called Xiaoxin Iron. French West nails are called iron wire nails. The purchasing season is every year at the end of the year and the beginning of the year, at the latest until April or May. After this, it is a period of stagnation. Transactions are either cash or term. It is stipulated during negotiations. The goods handled by the tea shops are handled by tea merchants in the mountains. The payment is advanced by the tea shops. Therefore, the tea shops have a deduction when purchasing goods. (That is, a handling fee of 0.995 or 0.9975). However, there are also cases where there is no deduction. Therefore, the seller must make it clear in advance, otherwise, there will be mistakes. The local companies that do this kind of business are Ke Chi, Yichang, Yuxianglong and other companies.

Free Discussion

"What good things can we show them?"

— Xuan

Children grow up year after year, and in addition to toys and snacks, they also ask for "spiritual food." Children of seven or eight years old are still easy to deal with; we have publications such as "Children's World" and "Little Friends." When they are eleven or twelve years old, they are no longer interested in stories about dog brothers and cat sisters, but they cannot understand general literary readings. So, the parents are very embarrassed.

Writers have already seen this point. The World Juvenile Literature Series and other similar books are published in response to this demand. But on the one hand, the quantity is not large, and on the other hand, the translation is too Europeanized, so the children's strong intellectual hunger cannot be satisfied. As a result, they find their own "way out": those with a higher level go to dig through old book piles, Seven Heroes and Five Gallants, Water Margin, Journey to the West, are still considered good. Those who are worse than that swallow all the cases of Shi Gong, the biography of Ji Gong, and all martial arts myths; children with a lower level regard "comic strip novels" as treasures. The children who have discovered their own "new world" feel that "Treasure Island," "King of the Golden River" and other similar books are boring, difficult to understand, and not to their taste.

"What good things can we show them?" Parents with ideas are probably often worried like this.

Some people have high standards and think that old novels with feudal consciousness such as Seven Heroes and Five Gallants are of course poisonous, and even Western juvenile literature such as "Treasure Island" is unhealthy, so children nowadays simply have nothing to read. This is naturally true. It's a pity that we can't give up eating because of choking. And children will secretly rent and watch all kinds of "poisons," and no method can stop it.

I think the immediate solution is——

Friends who are enthusiastic about children's literature unite to study why their releases are not enthusiastically liked by children.

Select relatively "hygienic" materials and compile or translate them in a planned way; but whether it is compiling or translating, don't make the language too Europeanized.

These are two principles. As for the specific methods, naturally, it needs full discussion. People who have children at home clamoring "want to read books" and authors who compile and translate children's books! Isn't this problem worth paying attention to?

Man-Made Earthquake

— Shiyi

When Bernard Shaw met with Minister Araki in Japan, Araki said to him: "It's a pity that you, old gentleman, didn't encounter an earthquake in Japan. Only after encountering an earthquake can you understand the superior national character of Japan." The old man Shaw's reply was: "If you were the Prime Minister of England, you would definitely bury bombs underground and create man-made earthquakes."

Although General Araki did not come to China to be the chairman, there are indeed many people in China who are processing and rushing to make man-made earthquakes.

Not to mention the imported and "domestic" airplanes, bombs, and tanks that are making earthquakes rumble in the "border areas" and "hinterland" every day. What about the foreign commodities that are flooding in and the incredible miscellaneous taxes, aren't they also shaking the countryside with man-made earthquakes. The people of Gansu and Shaanxi are destroying their own residences in order to avoid the army collecting housing taxes. This earthquake is already being made by themselves without waiting for it to be man-made. The army digs dikes due to attacks, and local tyrants embezzle public funds and do not repair dikes, forming a great flood that covers sixteen provinces, which is even more of a man-made tsunami following the man-made earthquake.

Araki thought that earthquakes cultivated the Japanese people and their superiority, which was for external development. In China, the result of this man-made earthquake has indeed cultivated the superiority of external development. For example, landlords in the interior move to concessions to be absentee landlords, and take their property to the safe deposit boxes of foreign banks. However, some people who have no homes to move to and no property to deposit seem to have no way to cultivate this kind of superiority, and can only groan in the man-made earthquake forever.

So, someone said: This is a "destined bitter life." Since "bitter life" is "destined," they have to wait for the mountains to collapse and the ground to crack, and be crushed to pieces!

Early Market

— Peng Xuezhen

Every morning, the bustling streets and alleys of this city are always flowing with so many people: all kinds of workers belonging to different classes, crawling like ants moving house before the rain. It's summer, and the south wind and the early dawn sky push people to the streets even earlier.

Vendors come one after another from the countryside or the docks, carrying burdens and panting, smiling at those who came earlier. This smile and hurried action implies a slight remorse: They are late. Selling bamboo shoots, selling fish, selling vegetables... scattered everywhere, everyone eagerly expects the customers who come to them, and always tries to gently grab him or her if the selling price has reached the point of agreement. The phrase "Okay, let's make a profit, I'll sell it to you!" contains the truth of life: People have to struggle to live. So the scale is busy, and the vendors carefully calculate how many pounds and taels and how many copper coins. This is more focused than the scholars sitting in the research room. There is no joking or mischief here, people are moving "seriously."

Every customer with a basket is busy looking for things: smart housewives are looking for cheap and good food, cooks are carefully calculating how to cater to the tastes of the owner, and people in rags who are pressed hard by life are discussing alone how to match the limited amount of copper coins with food and vegetables.

Everyone's feet crawl slowly like turtles lying in a basket. The apprentices opening the shop boards stare blankly at the people passing by on the street with greasy faces. The shouts of the carriers break the quiet air of the morning. The drivers chew on pancakes and fried dough sticks while waiting for business.

Everything seems to be planning for the blessed people, the street sweepers, the toilet pourers, the firewood ash collectors, and the "dry water" pourers are all people that the late-rising rich will never see and be disgusted by.

But these late-rising rich people will never have the opportunity to see these vivid pictures of the early market!

Little Black Girl

— Cao Juren

I knew Little Black Girl (not to be interpreted as "Little Black Girl knew me") twelve years ago, when she was about sixteen or seventeen years old. Her younger sister and brother were both studying at Cang Sheng Public School, which I was in charge of.

The White Girl storyteller in *The Travels of Lao Ts'an* made us yearn for such a thing. Hearing that there was a Black Girl storyteller at the New World entertainment center, I pretended to be refined and sat in the front row to drink tea and listen to the storytelling. Like "a Shandong person eating ophiopogon root," I didn't understand a thing. I only heard the sharp notes soaring high and the low notes sinking into the abyss, the rapid parts "like a cacophony of sounds," and the slow parts "like a warbling oriole flitting between branches," vaguely resembling the White Girl in Liu E's writing. Mr. Peixian said that Bai Yunpeng of the Great World entertainment center could be called a master of his time. I only felt that Bai Yunpeng had a very dignified demeanor, but I didn't understand anything else. Coincidentally, Mr. W worked at the New World, and we could enter and exit through the side door. We often went to listen to Little Black Girl's storytelling when we had free time.

Soon, Black Girl announced her retirement, and Little Black Girl took her place. Black Girl was not old, and Little Black Girl's skills were still raw and weak, a far cry from her predecessor. I wondered why one was retiring while such a child was taking the lead. Little Black Girl's eyes were dark and shiny. As soon as she stepped on stage, they would dart around, followed by cheers from several places. This situation was something that Black Girl's storytelling did not have. Previously, a few elderly people would applaud when the singing was particularly moving, but now many young people were applauding while their eyes were glued to her. One evening after Little Black Girl started performing, Mr. N called me to listen to the storytelling, saying, "The New World is especially lively tonight." Upon entering, I saw a packed house, and promotional flyers for Little Black Girl were flying everywhere. Little Black Girl would sing a line, and the audience would cheer. The storytelling that night was not particularly brilliant, but the amount of applause was unprecedented. There were three or five flower baskets on the stage, and a dozen or so banners, all praising Ms. Yang XX for her "three days around the beams" and "lofty mountains and flowing water." Little Black Girl's eyes were especially bright and darted around even faster that night.

One day, Little Black Girl brought her younger siblings to Cang Sheng Public School for class, and I learned that she lived nearby. Black Girl could also be seen from time to time. Over time, I realized that storytelling was not an interesting job. They could only eat half a bowl or a bowl of rice per meal, and they had to eat ten or so meals a day. They wouldn't be able to go to bed until after midnight, and they often stayed up until dawn when there were private performances. Lacking energy, they resorted to opium, which made them age even faster. Every time they arrived at a new port, they had to cater to the local "gentlemen," "powerful families," and "Ping opera professionals" to win their favor. Neither Black Girl nor Little Black Girl could read, but thanks to the care and attention they received, the Little Black Girl promotional flyers and the secret edition of Black Girl's drum lyrics appeared. (The "secret edition" was actually a tattered booklet with seventy to eighty percent of the characters misspelled.) "Though the peony is beautiful, it all depends on the green leaves to support it." Storytelling girls rely half on their skills and half on things "beyond their skills." Mr. Gao, a "Little Black Girl enthusiast," asked "Little Black Girl," "It's so 'good,' 'good,' does all that cheering make you cringe?" Little Black Girl was stunned for a moment and said, "Don't you writers need other people to cheer for you?" This stumped Mr. Gao.

After the Little Black Girl promotional flyers were flying everywhere, Little Black Girl's reputation soared, and she quickly became a very big "star." Everyone gradually forgot about Black Girl. Coincidentally, General Chen Shufan came from Shaanxi to Shanghai to enjoy his wealth from land speculation. A hero and a beauty, fulfilling a destined romance. It is said that Little Black Girl's storytelling skills also "improved day by day, reaching a state of perfection!"

A few days ago, I saw Little Black Girl at a storytelling venue in Beiping. Her aura was very different. Flower baskets were arranged in dense layers, and there were three to five hundred banners with "three days around the beams" and "lofty mountains and flowing water." It was like presenting a seal and worshiping a general, truly a pillar of the stage! Outside the door were two large characters: "Sold Out!" This couldn't help but make me think of "Black Girl" again! I once had a foolish thought: what would the author of *The Travels of Lao Ts'an* say if he were to ask from the underworld, "How was the White Girl back then?"

Carrot Whiskers

— by Jules Renard, translated by Lin Qu

Olorin

Mr. Lepic: How old are you now, Olorin?

Olorin: I turned sixty-seven on November 1st.

Mr. Lepic: So you're old, poor Olorin!

Olorin: As long as we can work, we don't feel old at all. I've never been sick. I think horses are not as sturdy as I am.

Mr. Lepic: Would you like me to tell you something, Olorin? You will die suddenly. One evening, returning from the river, you will feel that your back basket is too heavy, and the cart is not as easy to push as usual. You will kneel between the two cart arms, your nose stuck in the washed clothes, and then you will be done. By the time people pick you up, you will have already passed away.

Olorin: You're joking; please don't be afraid; my legs and arms are still strong.

Mr. Lepic: Your back is a bit hunched, that's true, but when your back is bent, washing clothes won't make your back ache so much. But your eyesight is failing, which is such a pity! Don't deny it, Olorin! I can see it.

Olorin: Ah! My eyes are as sharp as they were when I got married.

Mr. Lepic: Good! Then go open the cupboard and get me a plate, any plate will do. If you had wiped the dishes clean, then how would there be this moisture?

Olorin: The inside of the cupboard is a bit damp.

Mr. Lepic: Could it be that there are also some fingers touching the plates in the cupboard? Look at this fingerprint.

Olorin: Where is it, please show me, I didn't see it at all.

Mr. Lepic: That's exactly what I'm blaming you for, Olorin. Listen to me. I'm not blaming you for being lazy, if I said that, then I would be wrong; in our area, I haven't seen a second woman who works as hard as you; I'm just saying you're old. I'm the same, I'm old too; when we're old, we won't be able to do what we want. I can bet: you must often feel like there's a layer of cloth over your eyes. Even if you try your best to wipe it, it's still there on your eyes.

Olorin: But my eyes can open wide, and I don't feel like my head is submerged in water and my eyes are blurry. Mr. Lepic: Yes, yes, Olorin, you can believe what I say. Yesterday, you gave Mr. Lepic a dirty wine glass. I didn't say a word, because I was afraid of making you sad and causing a scene. Mr. Lepic didn't say a word either. He never says anything, but nothing can escape his eyes. People think he doesn't care, but that's wrong! He observes everything, but doesn't reveal anything. He just casually pushed your wine glass away with his finger, and he was even able to just eat without drinking. I was sad for you, and also sad for him.

Olorin: It's strange that Mr. Lepic would be so reserved in front of his own servant! He only needs to say a word, and I would replace the glass for him.

Mr. Lepic: That's true, Olorin, but even someone more cunning than you couldn't make Mr. Lepic, who is determined not to speak, talk. I don't even want to try it now. And the problem isn't here. In short: your eyesight is getting worse day by day. For rough work, like washing, it's not very important, but you can't do delicate work at all. Although expenses will increase, I would rather find someone to help you, if... (Unfinished)

Informal Discussions

Questions

— Niu

The saying goes, "A scholar doesn't step out of his gate, yet knows the affairs of the world." I truly admire the intelligence of scholars of the past. In the past, scholars didn't have newspapers to read, and yet they knew the affairs of the world. Now I run around every day and open the newspaper to read, but there are many things I don't understand when I read the news. I'm truly ashamed. Today I'll just bring up a few examples for consideration.

A Nanjing dispatch on the 7th stated that Dai Chuanxian invited over seventy teachers and students from Guangdong in Beijing to jointly transcribe Sun Yat-sen's Last Will and Testament. It was placed in a copper box, encased in a stone case, and a pagoda was built near the mausoleum to store it for posterity. At 8:00 AM on the 7th, a foundation-laying ceremony was held. When the stone case was being lowered from the top of the pagoda with a rope, the rope broke halfway and the case shattered. This is a strange event.

The Last Will and Testament of the Premier is extremely precious and should be stored in a famous mountain and passed on to future generations. Building a pagoda to store it is not unusual. But for such a grand ceremony, the equipment must have been carefully prepared. How could the rope have broken and the stone case shattered? It's truly incomprehensible.

Also, in a dispatch from the same day, Gao Youtang, a member of the Control Yuan, submitted an impeachment of Zhang Xueliang last month, accusing him of stealing ancient paintings from the Summer Palace. It stated, "Later, after Zhang Ji sent a stern telegram demanding their return, he admitted that they were stored in the Tianjin Concession. Even if they can be returned intact in the future, Zhang has already committed the crime of embezzlement under criminal law." After the Control Yuan sent it to Li Menggeng for review, he believed that it should be immediately handed over for disciplinary action and submitted it to the National Government to be handed over to the Central Public Servant Disciplinary Committee for disciplinary action. This matter is also a bit strange.

When Zhang Xueliang left, two cases of theft were discovered. One was the sale of the site of the Navy Hospital to a certain concession authority, and the other was the theft of ancient paintings from the Summer Palace. Now, Gao Youtang of the Control Yuan only impeaches Zhang Xueliang for stealing ancient paintings, but does not mention the sale of the Navy Hospital site. This is also incomprehensible.

In a dispatch from Beiping on the same day, this morning a Chinese youth entered a room in the Six Nations Hotel, fired two shots at an elderly Chinese man, seriously wounding him, and then calmly escaped in a car waiting outside the door. The name of the injured guest on the register was Zhang Shihang (actually Zhang Jingyao). He was sent to the German Hospital and died this afternoon. Strangely, Mr. Zhang himself denied being shot, claiming that his injury was caused by an electric shock.

Zhang Jingyao, as a traitor, knew that his crimes were heinous, so he changed his name to Shihang. Even after being assassinated this time, he could only admit his bad luck. It wouldn't be good to say that he was killed because he was a traitor. This is a trace of remaining conscience that the traitor showed when he was on his last breath, so he vehemently denied being shot. But it's incomprehensible why some unfilial children dressed him in a red-topped official hat, peacock feather, embroidered python robe, and a large dragon robe when Zhang was put in his coffin, making him look like a living traitor. They insist on presenting his stench, which is truly incomprehensible.

A Career Selling Writing

— Peng Nian

Selling writing: What an unpleasant and hated term!

. But for those so-called people who come out of universities today, in this society where "there's no place to give birth to me," it's really hard to find a better place than a career selling writing. Therefore, the number of people in society who live by selling writing is increasing day by day. The founding of newspapers and the addition of supplements are also developing like bamboo shoots after rain. Although this helps society and the country to some extent, it is also the only art of living for writers when they reach the end of their rope.

Because I was tormented by life and couldn't find a "place to live me," these two reasons forced me to embark on the path of selling writing. And only selling writing can live me. Now I take writing as my only way to survive. The supplements of newspapers are the most fertile place of production for me, and also the most precious and supreme "field" to "live me."

But selling writing is not easy: You pour out your heart and soul, rack your brains, write five or six hundred words, make it into an article, and you still have to prepay two cents for postage with no guarantee of a return. Then, whether the editor is destined to befriend you is still a question. Even if you have the greatest hope and it gets published, the reward is at most only one or two yuan. But how much of my heart and soul is lost in exchange for this one or two yuan reward! That's still good. Sometimes, to write an article, the tone must be a little激烈, otherwise you won't get the editor's sympathy. But the big men in the government just don't want to understand you, saying that you are from the XX faction, and immediately send a few detectives to monitor you, surrounding you, so you sigh that you can't move! If you're unlucky, you risk tasting the flavor of iron bars. Maybe they'll offer you a "sanitary pill." Wasn't Liu Yusheng our previous example?

Selling writing, although so scary! So painful! But my mouth is not getting any better, and my stomach is causing a storm. What method should I use to conquer it! For this reason, I can't care about so much anymore, I have to let myself drill into the hail of bullets to plan for my mouth.

The Young Ladies Are Silent

— Bing

The slightly warm spring breeze trembled all things on the earth. Although it was in a large city where spring came later, and although it was in a golden house with many gates and courtyards, one could still smell the mellow wine of spring. Every morning, the nanny would open the windows, letting in a new breath, and the young ladies would lazily stretch half their heads out of the quilt, "Oh, lovely spring morning!" After uttering a few charming words, they would get out of bed earlier than usual.

The eldest young lady's age, although she had passed twenty, still had the charm of a sixteen or seventeen-year-old girl in her prime. This was probably because she had never been married. She was already a junior in college, and had not only learned fluent Mandarin like a warbling oriole, but could also speak English. Her slender figure set off her white-red face, water-drop-like eyes, and small cherry lips. Every move was charming enough, and being a college student, her attitude was especially elegant. She was indeed worthy of pride and happiness.

The second young lady, although still a middle school student, was already in the sixth grade. Her age was just eighteen, and the flames of youth were burning fiercely in every cell of her. Her properly high nose bridge and apple-colored oval face were covered with two slender eyebrows, sheltering the autumn water-like eyes. Between glances, it was indeed enough to make people's souls flutter.

The youngest third young lady was only sixteen years old, but she could also speak English, because she attended a church middle school. Her face was full of childishness, always jumping around and never standing still. Although she was not as good at makeup and beautification as the eldest and second young ladies, she also revealed a natural girlish beauty.

Every day, when the young ladies went to college, a 1933 Ford car would separately pick them up and bring them back. They would jump into the courtyard, turn into the hall. The artificial wild scenery in the courtyard frequently smiled at them, and the flowers displayed in the hall spread their branches and leaves, composing a welcoming tune. The young ladies would take off their coats and chat and laugh as they pleased. One moment, the eldest young lady would teach the third young lady to sing English songs, followed by a graceful dance. Another moment, they would turn on the phonograph and play Western famous songs like "I LOVE YOU" and "March of the Soldiers." Then, they would eat and drink, and chat and laugh again. They were intoxicated in human paradise, truly happy and perfect.

Dusk approached, and the cries of newspaper vendors echoed outside the window. The young ladies suddenly remembered their movie night class. The eldest young lady, being a college student, said that she wanted to read the evening paper before going. So the nanny immediately bought an evening paper.

The atmosphere certainly changed quickly. The tide of joy that filled the entire room instantly vanished. The young ladies looked at each other, and everyone was silent. Fortunately, the nanny was standing beside them, and no matter what, they couldn't guess the truth of this mystery. "Such a perfect life for the young ladies, and yet they frowned, which is a bit ungrateful! Unjust!" The nanny murmured, and couldn't help but sneer, which made the eldest young lady furious and scolded her harshly, "Ignorant pest, get out!"

However, the clouds of sorrow still shrouded the faces of each of the young ladies, expressing endless depression that could not be resolved. Were they disgusted with the tyranny of the riot day? No! Were they mourning the martyred compatriots? No! Were they deeply resentful that the military men in charge of military power did not know how to defend the country, seeing the national situation in danger and the territory lost? No! Did they express regret after seeing that hundreds of laborers were killed by the explosion in the XX factory on Tangshan Road? No, it wasn't any of that!

It was because the eldest young lady's lover was in Chaoyang, Rehe, which had been lost, and it was really unknown whether he was good or bad. Moreover, Tianjin and Beijing were also facing a serious situation, and the lovers of the second and third young ladies were all in the dangerous city of Beiping!

Dinner Party

— Li Min

It was the time when the lights were just coming on, cars were humming, and people were noisy, especially showing the hustle and bustle of the city at night.

"Yipinxiang, Yizhixiang, Xinghualou, Taohuagong..." These many towering restaurants in the city were full of rich young men, and the pink stationery flew, and after a while, seventeen or eighteen-year-old girls flew in.

The young men just had a dinner party like this: calling a few games; what the poor could get by for half a year!

Behind Taohuagong, on a road that never saw the light; there were alleys built one after another

Page 20

, telling you that this was the home of goddesses in the civilized city, indeed; the alleys were shrouded in a lot of mystery!

At this time: under the overhanging building of an alley, there were five young masters disguised as civilized beggars! Sitting on the ground with their buttocks; round table meeting? No table! Dinner party? A bit like it:

The civilized beggars were all young! Their faces were thin and still had the strong color of the Philippines! The clothes sewn from red and green rags and coarse and fine sacks were worn on each person; they looked like the little Taoists in Xuanmiao Temple.

"Please: please; we all please," these civilized beggars! They all said this in their mouths, and the chopsticks were also casually thrown into several tin cans placed flat on the ground; but there was no sign of ferocity at all.

After they took this chopstick, they stopped talking again:

"This dinner party is much happier than last time."

"Yes; this is all the result of the efforts of the brothers!"

"When you say that; I feel nervous again! Dangerous! Yesterday, when I was overturning the yellow fish in the food stall in front of the Shenbao, I was almost caught by the red-headed devils!"

"The day before yesterday, I overturned the cold rice at Nichengqiao! And I was beaten by a foreign monkey!"

"Everyone is like this; these things all came from adventure!"

"That's right! Things that come from adventure taste especially good!"

The civilized beggars talked like this, one sentence from you; one word from me, and the delicacies in the several tin cans were gradually going down 丨 At this moment; suddenly a civilized beggar took out a paper package from his body, held it in his hand and said: "Yesterday I picked up a lot of flowers in front of a mansion! It's a pity that these flowers! They have been almost killed by them! I picked them up! I carefully wrapped them in newspaper, now I'll take them out for the brothers to appreciate, you can't touch them!" After saying that; he really unwrapped the paper package, which turned out to be several white orchid flowers!

The moon sister showed a smiling face, gradually rising to the center of the sky, and the noise of the city night slowly subsided! Under the overhanging building of an alley, several civilized beggars were sleeping haphazardly! Several snores were mixed together, meeting the breeze and stirring up, breaking the desolation of the night in the alley!

In a Certain University Dorm Room

— Pu Ru

A room full of laughter, a room full of footsteps, a room full of Jinghu fiddle sounds: xipi, erhuang, daoban… In the white dorm room, under the milky white electric light, three beds, four tables, a messy little bookshelf, a thermos on the table, a phonograph, and a pile of scattered paper, several pens, an overturned ink bottle, a woman's portrait, with "My heart!" and "Kiss me, endlessly!" written behind it! ...

"Hey, what movie did you see today?"

"Spring Breeze and Willow Branches, what about you?"

"Heartbreak."

"How was it?"

"The emotion was well expressed!"

People in suits, people in long gowns, people wearing hats, people wearing glasses, and people in pajamas crowded into the room. Jumping, standing, sitting, there were tall ones, short ones, pale-faced ones, dark ones…

"Hey, Old Chen, sing 'Si Lang Visits His Mother'."

"Hey, play, Old Zheng! Slow tempo xipi."

Then, the Jinghu fiddle suddenly changed its tune. "Yang YanHui, sits...in the palace..." Old Chen in a long gown began to sing, from "Si Lang Visits His Mother" to "Water Thrown Before the Horse," then to "Second Entry to the Palace"...

"Bravo!" Everyone cheered.

"I can't sing anymore, my vocal cords can't take it."

"Okay, I'll do it! You put on that...ah...ah..."

"No, let Old Li do it."

"Let's not play anymore, let's turn on the phonograph."

Opening the phonograph case, the machine was turned on, playing one record after another. Everyone sang along. "Ah, this daoban is sung so well!" Shaking his head.

"This, ah, ah, ah...the trailing tone is sung so skillfully!" Stomping his feet.

They were all amazed.

Only Little Xu with the hooked nose in pajamas was dancing alone; bored, he pulled Fat Zhu to dance with him, embracing him, dragging his feet on the floor. Then Old Huang with the crooked hat, Old Li with glasses, Old Zhou in a red suit, Little Wu with a pale face, and A Qin with a dark complexion all wanted to dance with him, embracing his waist, holding his hand... The dark-skinned one didn't know how to dance, so he pointed out his mistakes and taught him how to dance.

As they danced, the Jinghu fiddle started up again, quite smoothly. The phonograph was still singing ah, ah, ah, kuang, kuang, kuang, hei nong li dong..., but the sound was drowned out by the noise of the people, almost inaudible.

Dancing, singing loudly, laughing wildly, playfully fighting…

The door opened, and Old Hu with squinting eyes came in, carrying a stack of phonograph records and a bag of peanuts.

"GKKDNIGHTLFOODNIGHTL" Little Xu with the hooked nose in pajamas, leaving the dark-skinned one, went to greet him.

"Ha, ha, Old Hu!…"

With a whoosh, everyone rushed forward, snatching all the peanuts first. The Jinghu fiddle stopped playing, and everyone was laughing.

"Hey, what records did you bring?"

"Foreign dance records, foreign dance records."

"Okay, let's switch records."

The machine was turned on, and the foreign dance records were played.

"Come, come, we're still partners."

Little Xu with the hooked nose started dancing with Old Hu with squinting eyes. The electric light was covered with green paper, making it greenish, and it became their dance floor.

The foreign records played, and they embraced and danced: waltzes, foxtrots...

Their dance floor became a little quieter. Everyone watched with envy: they danced so skillfully!

Seeing others dance so well, their hands and feet itched. So Old Zheng playing the Jinghu fiddle, and Old Huang wearing a crooked hat, Old Li with glasses, and Fat Zhu: Old Zhou in a red suit, and Little Wu with a pale face: Old Chen in a long gown, and the dark-skinned one: all embraced, in pairs, and started dancing, crowding the room. There were tall ones, short ones, pale-faced ones, dark ones...

Dancing, dancing, smiling, singing foreign dance songs, greenish. ...

Suddenly, the electric light flickered, then lit up again, then flickered again, then lit up. Finally, it went out completely.

"Ah, the light's gone out."

"It's broken."

With a shout, they scattered in a rush.

In the corridor, the sound of shoes clattering. Everyone returned to their own dorm rooms, dark and silent.

"Hey, what are you taking tomorrow?"

"It's that damn French again."

"We have to take Civil Law and Land Law tomorrow."

Discussion on How to Be a Person

— Hui

This world is a world of the survival of the fittest, this world is a world of treachery. The Chinese are unbearable, and foreigners are bad too. I think we need to study and discuss how to be a person, even if this world is a world of love and harmony, this world is a world of justice, we should also study and discuss how to be a person. We can get along in this world. Mr. Fo, who used to write about the art of getting along in the attached publication, I think he was a misanthrope.

The first question in discussing how to be a person is whether it is better for us to be good people or bad people. I think it is better for us to be good people, because we ourselves do not like others to treat us badly, others to treat us with treachery, others to steal our things. We ourselves do not like to associate with people of bad character; we ourselves frown when we see people of bad character. Such people of bad character are everywhere not welcome. Confucius said, "Do not do to others what you do not want done to yourself," which is correct. Or some people say that being a bad person can take advantage of others. For example, when we trade with others, if we use heavy weights, we can take advantage of them. If we talk about morality and be good people, we will not be able to take advantage of others. I think this person is short-sighted! He doesn't know that if he always acts like this, perhaps before he even takes a step, everyone will break off relations with him, and it will be very difficult for him to stand in society. The advantage he gets is small and temporary, and the loss he suffers is great and long-lasting.

Now we discuss how to be a good person. We can get help from the books of Confucius and Mencius. Confucius and Mencius and other great Confucians were all great literary figures and masters of getting along in the world. An old gentleman said, "The Dao penetrates beyond the tangible universe, thoughts enter the changing forms of wind and clouds." How brilliant is his art of getting along in the world! This old gentleman is Mr. Cheng Hao. *The Travels of Lao Ts'an* and *Flowers in the Mirror* are considered good books by the world, and their authors both knew how to get along in the world.

Store Clerk Correspondence

Now I Know That Pickpockets are Not to Be Trifled With

Editor:

I know that you can answer all difficult questions, so I am writing with the utmost sincerity to ask you for a satisfactory answer.

I am an apprentice at a cigarette and paper shop in Caojiadu, Shanghai West, and I have been at the shop for almost a year. Our shop is located at a public bus stop, so pickpockets have emerged accordingly. In the past month, there have been many cases of people crying without recourse in front of the shop. Five days ago, a pickpocket stole an umbrella from a regular customer of our shop (commonly known as an old customer); two days ago, a pickpocket stole a wallet from another regular customer, worth about twenty yuan. It is said that this twenty yuan was for a debt that was about to expire, and if it was not returned, he would be ridiculed and scolded, which was unbearable. I saw this; I saw that his actions were suspicious, so I watched him. Later, an honest and sincere villager approached, using his hat to cover his face, and used light surgery to pickpocket the bag. At this time, I shouted "Pickpocket!" The villager was alerted, and the pickpocket knew that things were not going well, so he glared and raised his arm to leave. There was more than one person besides me who saw this. However, they all held to the principle of "If people don't offend me, I won't offend them." Alas, the world is like this, what more can be said?

Afterwards, some friends praised me for my courage, some ridiculed me for being nosy, and some worried about me, fearing that I would be harmed by villains. Time passed like lightning, and the god of night descended. The next morning, someone told me: The light in your store has been smashed to smithereens. Then there was a lot of discussion, some saying that villains should not be confronted, and some saying that petty theft is not worth mentioning. But I felt greatly uneasy in my heart, because my words had brought disaster to the shop, how could I not feel guilty? From now on, I know that pickpockets are not to be trifled with. Our shop is located at a public bus stop, and business is very good. We get up at 5:00 every morning and go to bed at 12:00 at night. Before 12:00, there was no loud noise, but the next morning the door lamp was on the ground, which proves that the lamp fell sometime after 12:00 and before 5:00. At this time, everyone in the shop was asleep, but did the patrol police on the street not hear anything?

Sir, my rambling words have been too much. Now, to sum up, how should pickpockets be dealt with? I can't bear to stand by and watch people in danger, but if I do, it will cause more trouble, not only making enemies with individuals, but also harming the shop. I am writing this letter especially to ask for your advice. (Below Omitted) Tang TieZheng

Editor's Note: "People should do their best to help the government prevent the occurrence of criminal acts." The laws of all countries have such provisions. So if you see a pickpocket stealing someone's things, it is a crime in principle not to take measures to stop it. However, Chinese law, because the people who made this law were inevitably influenced by the traditional poison of "Sweep the snow in front of your own door, and don't care about the frost on other people's roofs," did not clearly stipulate this meaning. Especially the clever Shanghai people, they really understand the art of getting along in the world, "If people don't offend me, I won't offend them." Even if they see someone about to be beaten to death, they will just walk away. What is it worth to have a pickpocket steal something? It is already unacceptable for ordinary people to hold this attitude. What is most regrettable is that the police officers who are responsible for preventing petty theft are also self-important and dare not offend illegal pickpockets.

If things continue like this, I dare say that in the near future, Shanghai will definitely become a world of pickpockets! So we admire Mr. Tang's actions very much; as for harming the shop owner, that was an accident. Justice will prevail over evil, and these pickpockets will not be able to make things too difficult for you. Moreover, pickpockets often patronize your old customers, which is not good for business, so a little sacrifice is not worth worrying about. We also want to advise everyone to stand up and do this, so that pickpockets can be eliminated. At the same time, the police officers who are responsible for preventing petty theft must also earnestly take responsibility and not turn a blind eye. Finally, I hope that when the criminal law is revised, the example of other countries will be followed and it will be clearly stipulated that "The people should do their best to help the government prevent the occurrence of criminal acts."

Novel

The Life of the Five Sisters (6) (Continued)

— Ling He

"Look at the hair on your chest!"

That was spring. It was very warm. People took off their gray squirrel fur and put on pearl-embroidered robes, but during the day, they still couldn't help but sweat.

The gate of Miss Liu's house had been decorated with red and green cloth since yesterday. Tonight, in addition to a bright gas lamp hanging over the main gate, there were also two octagonal glass lanterns. However, these were common sights in Beijing and were not particularly grand, so many people who passed by her house thought that something festive was happening inside, but they did not feel that it was particularly spacious. In Wu Gui's opinion, it shouldn't just be decorated like this. Since her master was so rich, why not spend more money to make the entrance more lively? But according to the master, it was not appropriate to be too extravagant in Beijing, as it would not sound good if people talked about it. Of course, Wu Gui didn't quite understand this. But if you went into Miss Liu's room, it was very different. Many of the furniture was made of rosewood, and the chair backs were carved with hollowed-out flowers and inlaid with Jiangxi porcelain panels painted with ink landscapes. The bed, of course, was a spectacle, and the copper pillars that gleamed with gold would emit a clear sound with just a light tap of a finger.

In addition, the white walls were hung with red satin happy curtains, and there was more than just one. There were also horizontal screens and couplets.

This day and night were very lively. After the formal wedding banquet, there was also card playing, a total of four tables. Because everyone was smoking cigarettes, whether it was Three Cannons or Double Knives, thick smoke always filled the air, even causing Miss Liu to wipe away tears with a handkerchief. At this time, a person with small eyes joked:

"What? Why is Xiao Liu crying? Don't you like Master Zhang? Don't underestimate him. Now that the Hongxian Emperor is about to ascend the throne, Master Zhang and his wife's brother are very close. You'll see, he'll become a minister in the future."

Originally, Miss Liu was sitting on Master Zhang's lap, playing cards for him, seemingly very happy, but after this person's teasing, she couldn't help but stand up and walk away from his arms. In fact, everyone knew that she wasn't crying. The guests finally left, and the house had a strange, unpleasant odor that was unique to the people in the house. So she pushed open a window facing the street, and a burst of women's laughter immediately flowed in with the cool air. It was the prostitutes who had just finished their shift and were going back.

Master Zhang sent the person out the door, then ran back into the room, hugged her tightly, and kissed her frantically, as if saying:

"Now I've finally got you!"

"Look at the hair on your chest!" she said softly to Master Zhang.

"Hahahaha!" Master Zhang laughed wildly. The smell of alcohol was on her face.

It was already dawn.

Film Special

How Did Films Really Begin? (Part 1)

— Shen Weng

Here is a more accurate answer!

There have been many different records about the origin of films. There are also conflicting opinions about who the original inventor of films was. Here is someone who, after various investigations, should indeed enjoy this honor. His name is William Friese-Greene, a photographer in London. His son, Claude Friese-Greene, recently worked for the British International Film Company and is now the most famous photographer in England. Below is what he wrote about the original state of film.

Although film has become a major part of people's lives in modern times, few people pay attention to how it began. If you ask any movie fan when film was invented, who the inventor was, or about the earliest sound films, you will surely get many bizarre answers. The inventor of film has been debated for many years. I can tell you that my father, William Friese-Greene, was the first to apply for and receive a patent for a motion picture camera. This was in June of 1889. He also went on to obtain a patent for making films, and he had unintentionally discovered the secret of moving pictures in 1885.

In 1880, my father conceived of the idea of combining Edison's phonograph with photography. From that time on, he spent years researching and trying to realize his ideal. In 1889, he even wrote to Edison about this plan, wanting to ask the American to cooperate with him in making sound films. Edison was clever and was of course very interested in this matter. He wrote back asking for the diagrams of the special camera to be sent to him, but there was no further communication after that.

My father had a deep interest in photography from a young age and was willing to study it. In 1882, he joined forces with John Arthur. Arthur had invented a projection lamp that could continuously capture scenes. My father's idea of moving pictures came from this lamp. He made various corrections to Arthur's invention. In 1885, he even held an exhibition at the British Photographic Society. Arthur died at this time, but my father continued his research.

For the next two years, he continued to work hard on research and improvement. He was a very famous photographer in London. Because of his reputation and credibility, when he held his "moving picture" exhibition in the laboratory, the audience was so crowded that the police had to intervene. (To be continued)

Film Commentary

Review of The Battle of Emden

— Shi Ming

The script still has some merit.

The performance is mediocre and lax.

"The Battle of Emden" (CIUISEREMDEN) was screened at Carlton, and about half of the audience was sailors from various countries. It was exported by a very famous German company, EMELKASTUOIO.

Although this is a work from three years ago, because it is a historical drama, there is nothing to criticize in its consciousness as being outdated or out of touch with the times. There is not much to talk about in the plot. It is only about the German warship "Emden" departing from Qingdao until it was destroyed and sunk by the British warship "Sydney." The first two parts slightly insert a love story, but it is minimal.

From beginning to end, it curses the evils and cruelty of war. The beginning is about soldiers leaving their wives and children to go to the front line, and it tries hard to write about the tragedy of separation and death. The interspersed love story is precisely to say that no matter what the environment, "love" is always selfish, and it frankly exposes the relationship between people. This film also fully describes the spirit of the German soldiers rushing into the flames and sacrificing themselves to save the ship. Of course, the German producers' propaganda of German courage and perseverance is very obvious.

Director Louis Ralph has greatly failed. With good historical materials, he can only tell a story plainly, and has no ability to dissolve it and turn it into a work of art. The segmentation of scenes is even more chaotic, making people dizzy, and sometimes it is not even clear whether this scene is of the Germans or the enemy [British]. The warship first has a big fire, then no fire, and finally it is completely burned, with a big loophole in the order.

The photography did use a lot of novel angles, but there is too little change. For example, there are more than ten shots of the sea "water," arranged in exactly the same way, making people feel very tired. There are too many small shots, so it is very trivial, and no scene has a delicate performance. The naval battle takes only long shots, which is very boring. The light is daylight, which is still clear. The sound is average. Too few people in China understand the German dialogue, which is also one of the reasons for the disappointment. As for the scenery, the interior and exterior scenes are both good, but the scene of "Emden" being destroyed is too obviously fake. The big fire scene can be said to be very tense.

A Tragic Epic Showcasing National Spirit

Produced by Youlian "Flower of Peace" starring Xu Qinfang

While "Emden" was in progress, three new-style destroyers appeared in the sea. These warships were completely from after 1925. They absolutely did not exist in 1914. This is also a big temporal oversight.

Using a map to show the "Emden's" journey is very clever, but according to actual reports, it destroyed as many as forty-two ships along the way. Now that the film has tried its best to be concise, and the map does not mention it at all, it is very inaccurate.

There is another advantage in this film, that is, the organization law of the navy. It seems that the director and actors have a lot of experience. But unfortunately, except for being destroyed, there is too little writing about the war.

The actors, each one mainly acts in combat, and the supporting roles and group work are still good.

Review of "Female Zhuge Liang" ALADYS PROTESSION

— Ling He

If we only consider the translated title "Female Zhuge Liang," one would inevitably assume that this woman must possess "divine intelligence and brilliant strategies," with "the universe in her sleeves," naturally "devising strategies in the command tent, and winning battles a thousand miles away." However, after spending a dollar to watch it with rapt attention, this Mrs. Zhuge Liang did not impress us enough to make us admire her.

In reality, this is a "common" film from Paramount. If we must rack our brains to find some meaningful merit, then the author of this film lightly mocks the declining baron, gentlemen who treat alcohol as their second life (desperately stealing drinks during Prohibition), and despicable bootleggers, etc. However, this mockery is by no means a servant expressing dissatisfaction with the "ungentlemanly" behavior of his master, but rather a humble person kneeling at the master's "feet" saying: "Dear master, please work hard to honor your ancestors, the glory of the old master still needs you to carry it forward!" However, whether this kowtowing and bowing can "turn the tide" and "establish the family's foundation" is a big question.

The structure of the story can be considered self-consistent. The young man and woman falling in love at first sight is, of course, the most successful writing style of American films, and this film naturally has its share of it. But love words, hugs, and secret marriages, based on past experience, can indeed make money.

The director certainly worked very hard on this film. Look, he actually turned such a story into such a movie. In order to make well-fed people come to the cinema for entertainment, he made the ridiculous dialogues particularly loud. Action "gags" are, of course, even more necessary, so a dwarf carves fountain pens or STICKs with a small knife, and a horse's hoof crushes a gentleman's top hat ("this also has a bit of satirical meaning"), and they are filmed again and again, and again and again. These kinds of jokes are fundamentally very "laughable."

The "old-fashioned and arrogant" "old star" ALISON SKIPWORTH is certainly "old-fashioned" enough, and her performance is not bad. She is comparable to Marie Dressler, who starred in comedy films like "Female Politician," but she is not necessarily "arrogant." ROLAND YOUNG, who starred in "The Gay Divorcee," is still both funny and annoying here. GEORGE BARBIER, who plays the rich man, is quite thought-provoking. SARIMARITZA is indeed very beautiful, although her performance is not successful.

The sound quality is sometimes chaotic. The set design is passable... In short, this is a mediocre film.

George Brent's Dimming Eyesight Mei Cun

The news about George Brent's failing eyesight has been circulating in Hollywood for quite some time. They seem to feel very sorry for this Irish opera singer's misfortune, especially at a time when he is enjoying great fame in the film industry.

The only reason is said to be the effect of KLEIGLIGHTS, but on the other hand, it is also blamed on his excessive reading as a child without paying attention to the root cause planted. George came to the United States to pursue a life on the stage. Because he was the protagonist, he had to carefully read the scripts every week. As a result, the strong lights often fatigued his eyes' ability to adjust, leading to a state of stagnation. Moreover, during the day, he did not protect his eyes with sunglasses, so his eyesight deteriorated further.

When he realized the trouble with his eyesight, he wanted to take a period of rest, but as luck would have it, Warner Bros.' executives took a fancy to him at this time and begged him to join the film industry. Since he had long had this ambition for film, he naturally agreed and put the major matter of rest out of his mind. He repeatedly played opposite female leads such as Ruth Chatterton, Constance Bennett, Joan Blondell, and Loretta Young, and his reputation grew day by day.

However, his eye disease also worsened. After marrying Ruth Chatterton last year, she advised him to rest, but his interest in film and the praise he received continued to fascinate him. As a result, he only hired a doctor to be his consultant.

"Cosmetic Market" Soon to be Released

— Jing

Because of the release of "Freedom Flower", Hu Die has gained even more audience admiration. Now, her second sound film after "Freedom Flower," "Cosmetic Market," which she also stars in, will soon be released.

In "Cosmetic Market," Ms. Hu Die plays a young woman from a semi-feudal family who, due to the pressure of circumstances, has to seek employment, and thus enters a department store as a female employee. However, once she enters society, many unexpected disputes surround her, even pushing her to the wall. Inside, there are descriptions of the female employees' jealousy and fighting, and the absurd and licentious pleasures of young masters and company supervisors, etc. The power of exposure can be said to be extremely strong.

Of course, out of a passion for supporting domestic films, the release of "Cosmetic Market" is something we should be happy about!

Film Novel Secrets (SECRETS) (5)

— Cairo

"Who else's cows are in your house?" Jack said, and laughed heartily.

"You are so hateful," Mary shouted resolutely, "My husband has worked so hard all this time, only to have you thieves rob him. You robbers, murderers!"

Jack listened, his eyes half-closed, and suddenly pulled out a sharp knife from his waist. He threw it forward, and it stuck into the wooden bed just inches away from little John's head. Mary cried out in alarm and quickly picked up little John. Jack said, "Next time you speak, be careful. And remember, my knife never misses." With that, they left.

Mary hugged her child and wept. John and Shen Xiang returned. They had already encountered Jack and his gang of robbers on the road, but because the odds were so uneven, and they were worried about Mary and the child's safety, they did not fight them but quietly let them pass. John returned home and discussed with Mary the plan to move to a better place. Mary still suspected that he was weak, willing to be chased away so easily by a gang of robbers. John wanted to tell her what kind of people these cattle thieves were and why they couldn't resist with force; but as his eyes wandered around, he saw the little wooden cow lying on the ground, crushed by leather boots; and at little John's bedside, stuck a sharp little knife. When he saw it, anger flooded his heart like a tide, and he could no longer hold it back. These hateful thieves not only stole his cattle, but also invaded his home! This was intolerable! He jumped up suddenly, grabbed his gun from the stool, and slung it over his shoulder. He said, "Mary, you are right. I can't be chased away so easily by a bunch of thieves. In this village, we can still find a dozen strong men to fight them to the death." He hugged her in his arms and said softly, "I may not be back tonight, but Shen Xiang will help you watch the house." He walked over, pulled out Jack's knife, stuck it in his belt, and strode to the door.

"Dear John, I love you," Mary called out softly behind him. As he walked out the door, she looked at her husband's back, her heart filled with infinite pain and pride. Then she closed the door and returned to her son's side.

John did not return for three days. During these three days, Mary felt shrouded in sorrow and darkness at home. Little John was very ill. Mary had no choice but to send Shen Xiang to the neighboring village to fetch Dr. McGoffin. Mary and Dr. McGoffin took turns caring for little John. Later, little John had a glimmer of hope for survival, and Mary felt much more at ease, but the doctor warned her: "Little John's heart is still very fragile, and he must not be frightened in the slightest, nor should he hear any loud noises. Otherwise..."
